format\n\n\npath_map.csv\n\n\nold_root,new_root\n\\\\OLD-SERVER\\GISShare,\\\\NEW-SERVER\\GISShare\nD:\\OldData,\\\\NEW-SERVER\\GISData\n\n\nPython (run in ArcGIS Pro’s Python environment)\n\n\n# /scripts/repoint_aprx_datasources.py\n\"\"\"\nRepoint ArcGIS Pro APRX layer/table data sources using an old_root -> new_root mapping CSV.\n\nRun:\n  - Inside ArcGIS Pro: Python window, or\n  - As a standalone script using ArcGIS Pro's Python environment.\n\nCSV columns:\n  old_root,new_root\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport argparse\nimport csv\nimport os\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass\nfrom typing import Iterable\n\nimport arcpy\n\n@dataclass(frozen=True)\nclass PathMap:\n    old_root: str\n    new_root: str\n\ndef _norm(p: str) -> str:\n    # Normalize for Windows/UNC comparisons (case-insensitive)\n    return os.path.normpath(p).rstrip(\"\\\\/\").lower()\n\ndef load_path_map(csv_path: str) -> list[PathMap]:\n    maps: list[PathMap] = []\n    with open(csv_path, \"r\", newline=\"\", encoding=\"utf-8-sig\") as f:\n        reader = csv.DictReader(f)\n        if not reader.fieldnames or \"old_root\" not in reader.fieldnames or \"new_root\" not in reader.fieldnames:\n            raise ValueError(\"CSV must have headers: old_root,new_root\")\n        for row in reader:\n            old_root = (row.get(\"old_root\") or \"\").strip()\n            new_root = (row.get(\"new_root\") or \"\").strip()\n            if old_root and new_root:\n                maps.append(PathMap(old_root=old_root, new_root=new_root))\n    # Longest old_root first so deep paths match before shallow ones\n    maps.sort(key=lambda m: len(_norm(m.old_root)), reverse=True)\n    return maps\n\ndef apply_mapping(path: str, maps: Iterable[PathMap]) -> tuple[str, bool]:\n    p_norm = _norm(path)\n    for m in maps:\n        o = _norm(m.old_root)\n        if p_norm == o or p_norm.startswith(o + os.sep.lower()) or p_norm.startswith(o + \"\\\\\"):\n            # Replace using the original string to preserve original casing after root\n            replaced = path.replace(m.old_root, m.new_root, 1)\n            return replaced, True\n    return path, False\n\ndef iter_layers_and_tables(aprx: arcpy.mp.ArcGISProject):\n    for m in aprx.listMaps():\n        for lyr in m.listLayers():\n            yield (\"layer\", m.name, lyr)\n        for tbl in m.listTables():\n            yield (\"table\", m.name, tbl)\n\ndef update_item(item, maps: list[PathMap], validate: bool, dry_run: bool) -> tuple[bool, str, str]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Returns: (changed, before, after)\n    \"\"\"\n    if not item.supports(\"DATASOURCE\"):\n        return False, \"\", \"\"\n\n    before = item.dataSource  # may throw for some layer types; supports() check reduces that risk\n    after, changed = apply_mapping(before, maps)\n\n    if not changed:\n        return False, before, before\n\n    if dry_run:\n        return True, before, after\n\n    # For most file/fgdb/sde cases, string-based updateConnectionProperties works.\n    # validate=False is safer during bulk edits; you can validate later in Pro.\n    try:\n        ok = item.updateConnectionProperties(before, after, validate=validate)\n    except TypeError:\n        # Some Pro versions accept positional args only\n        ok = item.updateConnectionProperties(before, after, validate)\n\n    if not ok:\n        raise RuntimeError(f\"updateConnectionProperties returned False for: {before} -> {after}\")\n\n    return True, before, after\n\ndef main() -> int:\n    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()\n    parser.add_argument(\"--aprx\", required=True, help=\"Path to .aprx\")\n    parser.add_argument(\"--path-map-csv\", required=True, help=\"CSV with old_root,new_root\")\n    parser.add_argument(\"--out-aprx\", default=\"\", help=\"Output .aprx path (optional). If omitted, overwrites input.\")\n    parser.add_argument(\"--validate\", action=\"store_true\", help=\"Validate connections during update (slower).\")\n    parser.add_argument(\"--dry-run\", action=\"store_true\", help=\"Print changes only; do not save.\")\n    args = parser.parse_args()\n\n    maps = load_path_map(args.path_map_csv)\n    if not maps:\n        raise ValueError(\"No mappings loaded from CSV.\")\n\n    aprx = arcpy.mp.ArcGISProject(args.aprx)\n\n    changes = []\n    for kind, map_name, item in iter_layers_and_tables(aprx):\n        try:\n            changed, before, after = update_item(item, maps, validate=args.validate, dry_run=args.dry_run)\n        except Exception as ex:\n            changes.append((kind, map_name, getattr(item, \"name\", \"<unnamed>\"), \"ERROR\", str(ex)))\n            continue\n\n        if changed:\n            changes.append((kind, map_name, getattr(item, \"name\", \"<unnamed>\"), before, after))\n\n    # Report\n    if changes:\n        print(f\"Found {len(changes)} item(s) needing attention.\")\n        for kind, map_name, name, before, after in changes:\n            print(f\"\\n[{kind.upper()}] Map: {map_name} | Name: {name}\")\n            print(f\"  BEFORE: {before}\")\n            print(f\"  AFTER : {after}\")\n    else:\n        print(\"No changes needed.\")\n\n    if args.dry_run:\n        print(\"\\nDry-run mode: nothing saved.\")\n        return 0\n\n    out_aprx = args.out_aprx.strip() or args.aprx\n    if out_aprx != args.aprx:\n        aprx.saveACopy(out_aprx)\n        print(f\"\\nSaved copy: {out_aprx}\")\n    else:\n        aprx.save()\n        print(f\"\\nSaved: {out_aprx}\")\n\n    return 0\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    raise SystemExit(main())\n\n\nNotes (important in practice):\n\n\nThis targets map layers and map tables (the most common breakage).\n\nModelBuilder path repair is usually separate because model tool parameters store paths differently than map layer sources.\n\n\n\nWhat I need from you next (so I can be precise without guessing)\n\n\nWhen you’re ready, paste/attach any of the following and I’ll give exact steps/code tailored to your setup:\n\n\nThe old root and new root paths (UNCs), and whether drive letters were involved\n\nWhether broken items are mostly map layers, ModelBuilder, or both\n\nYour ArcGIS Pro version (e.g., 3.x) and whether enterprise .sde connections are involved\n\n\na. Windows-readonly, (3) can Pro open/save the project, (4) is the default GDB writable (creates/deletes a tiny test FC).\n\n\n# /scripts/check_aprx_writable.py\n\"\"\"\nArcGIS Pro (ArcPy) diagnostics for \"project is read-only\" issues.\n\nWhat it checks:\n1) Project file exists and Windows \"Read-only\" attribute.\n2) Project folder write/delete test.\n3) Can open APRX and save (or save a copy).\n4) Default geodatabase path and write/delete test (CreateFeatureclass + Delete).\n\nRun (ArcGIS Pro Python):\n  python check_aprx_writable.py --aprx \"\\\\\\\\10.0.0.157\\\\esri\\\\LawEnforcementDataManagement_New\\\\LawEnforcementDataManagement.aprx\"\n\nOptional:\n  --save-copy \"C:\\\\Temp\\\\LawEnforcementDataManagement_copy.aprx\"\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport argparse\nimport os\nimport stat\nimport sys\nimport uuid\n\nimport arcpy\n\ndef is_windows_readonly(path: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Return True if the Windows read-only attribute is set (best-effort).\"\"\"\n    try:\n        mode = os.stat(path).st_mode\n        return not bool(mode & stat.S_IWRITE)\n    except OSError:\n        return False\n\ndef write_delete_smoke_test(folder: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:\n    \"\"\"Try create+delete a file in folder.\"\"\"\n       "say": "Svg Vector Icons : http://www.onlinewebfonts.com/icon\n\n\nYou’re running into a quirky ArcGIS Pro/ArcPy edge case: some “Layer” objects returned by listLayers() don’t support .name (it happens with certain internal/temporary layer types). Your earlier inventory worked because it only touched dataSource on those; this removal script hit .name and crashed.\n\n\nFix: never assume .name exists.       "say": "Svg Vector Icons : http://www.onlinewebfonts.com/icon\n\n\nYou’re super close — aprx.toolboxes is returning a list of dicts, not plain strings. So you need to pull out the toolboxPath value before importing.\n\n\nAlso: arcpy.ImportToolbox() changes the GP “tool namespace”; ListTools() can be noisy and not scoped the way you expect. For our purpose (find broken paths), it’s better to:\n\n\nlist toolbox paths correctly, and\n\nsearch inside the .atbx contents for old UNC strings / invalid paths.\n\n\n1) Paste this: list toolbox paths correctly\n\n\nimport arcpy\n\naprx = arcpy.mp.ArcGISProject(\"CURRENT\")\n\nprint(\"=== Toolboxes (normalized) ===\")\ntbx_paths = []\n\nfor item in (aprx.toolboxes or []):\n    if isinstance(item, dict) and \"toolboxPath\" in item:\n        tbx_paths.append(item[\"toolboxPath\"])\n        print(item[\"toolboxPath\"])\n    else:\n        # fallback if Pro returns strings in other environments\n        tbx_paths.append(str(item))\n        print(str(item))\n\nprint(\"=== Done ===\")\n\n\n2) Paste this: scan .atbx files for UNC/file paths and report missing ones\n\n\nThis is the most reliable approach across Pro versions because .atbx is a SQLite container (binary-ish), but it still stores many paths as text. We’ll do a safe “strings” scan and validate candidates.\n\n\nimport os\nimport re\nimport arcpy\n\naprx = arcpy.mp.ArcGISProject(\"CURRENT\")\n\ndef get_toolbox_paths():\n    paths = []\n    for item in (aprx.toolboxes or []):\n        if isinstance(item, dict) and \"toolboxPath\" in item:\n            paths.append(item[\"toolboxPath\"])\n        else:\n            paths.append(str(item))\n    return paths\n\ndef read_bytes(path):\n    with open(path, \"rb\") as f:\n        return f.read()\n\ndef extract_ascii_strings(blob, min_len=8):\n    # crude but effective: find runs of printable ASCII that often contain paths\n    return re.findall(rb\"[ -~]{%d,}\" % min_len, blob)\n\ndef looks_like_path(s):\n    s = s.strip()\n    return (\n        s.startswith(\"\\\\\\\\\") or\n        re.match(r\"^[A-Za-z]:\\\\\", s) or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".gdb\") or\n        \".gdb\\\\\" in s.lower() or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".sde\") or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".shp\") or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".csv\") or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".xlsx\") or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".tif\") or\n        s.lower().endswith(\".tiff\")\n    )\n\ndef normalize_candidate(s):\n    s = s.replace(\"/\", \"\\\\\")\n    # strip obvious wrappers\n    s = s.strip(' \"\\'')\n    return s\n\ndef existing_path_prefix(p):\n    # For feature class paths like \\\\server\\share\\something.gdb\\FC, check the gdb folder too\n    low = p.lower()\n    if \".gdb\\\\\" in low:\n        gdb = p[:low.index(\".gdb\\\\\") + 4]\n        return [p, gdb]\n    return [p]\n\nprint(\"=== Scanning .atbx for path references ===\")\n\ntbx_paths = get_toolbox_paths()\nif not tbx_paths:\n    print(\"No toolboxes registered in the project.\")\nelse:\n    for tbx in tbx_paths:\n        print(f\"\\n[TOOLBOX] {tbx}\")\n        if not os.path.exists(tbx):\n            print(\"  ! Toolbox file not found on disk.\")\n            continue\n\n        blob = read_bytes(tbx)\n        strings = [b.decode(\"utf-8\", errors=\"ignore\") for b in extract_ascii_strings(blob, min_len=12)]\n\n        # Filter to likely paths and dedupe\n        candidates = []\n        seen = set()\n        for s in strings:\n            s = normalize_candidate(s)\n            if not looks_like_path(s):\n                continue\n            if s in seen:\n                continue\n            seen.add(s)\n            candidates.append(s)\n\n        if not candidates:\n            print(\"  (No obvious path-like strings found.

)\")\n            continue\n\n        missing = []\n        for c in candidates:\n            exists_any = False\n            for p in existing_path_prefix(c):\n                if os.path.exists(p):\n                    exists_any = True\n                    break\n            if not exists_any:\n                missing.append(c)\n\n        print(f\"  Found {len(candidates)} path-like string(s). Missing on disk: {len(missing)}\")\n        for m in missing[:50]:\n            print(f\"    [MISSING] {m}\")\n        if len(missing) > 50:\n            print(f\"    ... ({len(missing)-50} more)\")\n\nprint(\"\\n=== Done ===\")\n\n\nHow to interpret results\n\n\nIf you see missing UNC paths that look like the old server/share, that’s where ModelBuilder/tools are still pointing.\n\nIf missing is 0, your toolboxes are likely clean (or the paths are stored in a way that doesn’t surface via string scanning—less common).\n\n\n\nIf you want to actually list tools/models (optional)\n\n\nWe can do it too, but it depends on Pro version/ATBX behavior. Keep it readable in Python window\n        u = (u or \"\").strip().replace(\"\\r\\n\", \"\\n\")\n        if len(u) > 400:\n            u = u[:400] + \" ...[truncated]\"\n        return True, u\n    except Exception as ex:\n        return False, f\"{type(ex).__name__}: {ex}\"\n\nprint(\"=== Import tbx1 ===\")\narcpy.ImportToolbox(TBX1, \"tbx1\")\nprint(\"[PASS] Imported\")\n\ntools = arcpy.ListTools(\"*_tbx1\") or []\nprint(f\"\\n=== Tools found: {len(tools)} ===\")\n\nfor raw in tools:\n    base = raw[:-5] if raw.lower().endswith(\"_tbx1\") else raw  # strip suffix\n\n    candidates = [\n        raw,\n        base,\n        \"tbx1.\" + base,\n        TBX1 + \"\\\\\" + base,\n        TBX1 + \"\\\\\" + raw,\n    ]\n\n    print(f\"\\n[TOOL] raw='{raw}' base='{base}'\")\n    resolved = False\n\n    for cid in candidates:\n        ok_d, info_d = try_describe(cid)\n        ok_u, info_u = try_usage(cid)\n\n        # Consider it \"resolved\" if either Describe or Usage works\n        if ok_d or ok_u:\n            resolved = True\n            print(f\"  id: {cid}\")\n            if ok_d:\n                print(f\"  Describe: {info_d}\")\n            else:\n                print(f\"  Describe: (no) {info_d}\")\n            if ok_u:\n                print(f\"  Usage:\\n{info_u}\")\n            else:\n                print(f\"  Usage: (no) {info_u}\")\n            break\n\n    if not resolved:\n        print(\"  ! first\n    strong = [\n        \"incidentid\", \"incident_id\", \"incidentnumber\", \"incident_number\",\n        \"caseid\", \"case_id\", \"casenumber\", \"case_number\",\n        \"reportid\", \"report_id\", \"reportnumber\", \"report_number\",\n    ]\n    for c in strong:\n        if c in lower_map:\n            return lower_map[c]\n\n    # Heuristic: any field containing incident/case + id/number\n    ranked = []\n    for n in names:\n        nl = n.lower()\n        score = 0\n        if \"incident\" in nl:\n            score += 5\n        if \"case\" in nl:\n            score += 4\n        if \"report\" in nl:\n            score += 3\n        if nl.endswith(\"id\") or \"_id\" in nl:\n            score += 4\n        if \"number\" in nl or nl.endswith(\"no\") or nl.endswith(\"num\"):\n            score += 3\n        if score > 0:\n            ranked.append((score, n))\n    ranked.sort(reverse=True, key=lambda x: x[0])\n    return ranked[0][1] if ranked else
